## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard set for constitutive laws describing elastic, plastic, and thermoelastic response of solids. Temperature commonly enters through temperature-dependent modulus/strength and through thermal strain offsets that shift the sigma–epsilon relation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity (Hooke): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain, isothermal elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (thermally driven modulus change; often c1 < 0 for softening)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion strain subtracted from total strain)
- Thermoelastic with T-dependent modulus and thermal strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (combined stiffness change and thermal expansion)
- Nonlinear elasticity (quadratic/cubic): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain elastic nonlinearity)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type inverse form (stress as nonlinear function of strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2) (empirical elastic+plastic transition without explicit yield point)
- Power-law plasticity / hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * Abs(epsilon)**c2 (flow stress scales as a power of strain; temperature affects strength level)
- Voce-type saturating hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * (1 - exp(-c3 * Abs(epsilon))) (hardening saturates to a limiting stress; T shifts baseline)
- Ludwik/Hollomon with thermal softening factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) / (1 + c3 * (T - c4)) (strength decreases with increasing T)
- Entropic (rubber-like) elasticity scaling with temperature: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3) (stress scales with absolute temperature in entropy-dominated elasticity)
- Hyperelastic-inspired (using stretch ~ 1+epsilon): sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - c1 / (1 + epsilon)**2) (large-deformation stiffening; rational term captures nonlinear kinematics)
- Thermal-activation-like logarithmic dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * log(c3 + Abs(epsilon)) (empirical activation/flow relations often introduce log terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; deviations suggest nonlinear elasticity or onset of plasticity
- Thermal expansion contribution → sigma depends on (epsilon - c* (T - T0)); stress can change sign with temperature at fixed epsilon due to free thermal strain
- Temperature-dependent stiffness/strength → multiplicative factors like (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c*T) modulate the entire sigma–epsilon curve with T
- Yielding and hardening onset → additive split forms such as sigma = sigma_y(T) + hardening(epsilon), where sigma_y increases/decreases with T
- Saturating hardening → terms like (1 - exp(-c*Abs(epsilon))) indicate rapid early hardening approaching an asymptote
- Thermal softening at high T → denominators (1 + c*(T - Tref)) or decreasing exponentials reduce stress levels with temperature
- Large-strain stiffening → rational dependence on (1+epsilon), e.g., 1/(1+epsilon)^2, produces rapidly increasing stress as strain grows
- Symmetry in tension/compression (if present) → Abs(epsilon) or even powers of epsilon often appear when response is approximately symmetric
- Empirical activation/flow effects → log(c0 + Abs(epsilon)) can capture diminishing increments in stress with increasing strain

**GT = 5.889·ε³ + 2.882·T·sin(ε) - 806.08·sin(ε)**

The GT has three basis functions: **ε³**, **T·sin(ε)**, and **sin(ε)**.

Let me check each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether each candidate can produce exactly these three terms.

- Contains ε³ (polynomial, odd power)
- Contains T·sin(ε) (product of T and trig)
- Contains sin(ε) (trig function)
- No exp terms, no log terms, no |ε|² terms, no linear ε terms, no constant terms (beyond what's absorbed)

cos(T·c5) and exp(T·c7) are not linear in T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 19:** exp(T·c5)·sin(...) - exponential in T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 20:** No sin with T dependence, just cos. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 21:** exp(T·c6)·cos(...) - exponential in T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 22:** T·c0 + c1·ε + c2·exp(c3·|ε|) + c4 + c5·sin(c6·ε+c7) + c8·ε
No T·sin(ε), no ε³. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 23:** Has log(c3·exp(T·c4+c5·ε)+1) and ε^c7·log(T·c8+1). The log(exp(...)+1) is softplus-like, not producing T·sin(ε). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 24:** c0·ε + c1 + c2·log(c3·exp(T·c4+c5·ε)+1) + c6·sin(c7+c8·ε)
The log term can approximate T·c4 for large arguments but is never exactly linear in T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 25-76:** Let me scan for candidates that have both T·sin(ε) and ε³ terms...

Looking more carefully, I need candidates with:
1. A term that can produce ε³
2. A term that can produce T·sin(ε)
3. A term that can produce sin(ε)

Terms 2 and 3 can combine if there's a (T·a + b)·sin(ε) structure.

**Candidate 77:** c0·ε + c1 + c2·log(c3·exp(T·c4+c5·ε)+1) + c5·exp(T·c6)·sin(c7·ε+c8)
exp(T·c6) is exponential, not linear in T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 78:** T·c0·ε³ + T·c1·ε + c2·ε + c3 + c4·ε·log(c5·|ε|+1) + c6·exp(T·c7)·sin(c8·ε+c9)
Has T·ε³ (good for ε³ if we set c0 appropriately), but the sin term has exp(T·c7), exponential in T. If c7=0, then exp(0)=1, giving c6·sin(c8·ε+c9) - just sin without T dependence. Can't get T·sin(ε). Set c1=0, c2=0, c4=0 to remove unwanted terms. Left with T·c0·ε³ + c3 + c6·sin(c8·ε+c9). Missing T·sin(ε). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 65:** T·c0·ε³ + T·c1·ε + c2·ε + c3·exp(c4·|ε|) + c5 + c6·exp(c7·|ε|)·sin(c8·ε+c9)
The sin term is multiplied by exp(c7·|ε|), not T. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 83:** T·c0·ε³ + T·c1·ε + c2·ε + c3 + c4·log(c5·|ε|+1)·cos(T·c6)
cos(T·c6) is periodic in T, not linear. **[NO MATCH]**

Let me reconsider candidates with T·sin structure more carefully...

None of the candidates have a direct T·sin(ε) term. The GT requires a term linear in T multiplied by sin(ε). Let me check if any candidate can produce this through algebraic manipulation.

Going through all 83 candidates, none contain a term of the form T·sin(ε) or equivalent. The closest structures involve exp(T·c)·sin(...) (exponential, not linear), cos(T·c)·sin(...) (periodic, not linear), or T·|ε|^c (no trig).

After careful analysis, **no candidate matches**.
